<U>Messages<UC><C><L.36.1>
<L.6.1>
<Z>Playoff Keys and Bonuses <C> I'm still keen for feedback on the possibility of making a change to way keys and bonuses work in<L.31.1>
the playoffs. Thus far I've not had much, and it may be a case of "if it ain't broke, don't fix it".<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
During the regular season, you have one key player and one bonus player per opponent, plus one bonus skill (which applies to the<L.31.1>
whole team) which seems to me to be perfectly logical. Once you get into the playoffs, the decision making process gets rather<L.31.1>
simpler - you have the same opponent for all (two or) three series so many coaches apply the same bonuses and key for each series<L.31.1>
(though the bonus skill varies more often, based on the stadium type). Combined with the fact that you don't have injuries to<L.31.1>
contend with (which I don't propose to change) and probably not fatigue either it's all rather automatic, and gives you rather<L.31.1>
fewer decisions to make.<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
My suggestion is that you should still have three player keys for the playoffs, but that all three keys will apply for every game<L.31.1>
(on a sliding scale, so the first key is more effective than the second, and that more effective than the third). The same would<L.31.1>
apply with the bonus player, but not the bonus skill (so you could still "neutralise" a key with a bonus if you choose - a player<L.31.1>
bonused by you and keyed by your opponent plays "as normal", but obviously your bonus is used up). It'll give you more decisions<L.31.1>
to make, and is probably more realistic too. During the regular season teams play one opponent for three days, then move on, and<L.31.1>
there aren't too many opportunites for your coaching staff to make specific adjustments for particular opponents (which is what<L.31.1>
keys and bonuses are meant to reflect). However, during the playoffs a team have 7-10 days against one particular opponent, so<L.31.1>
it's rather more logical that they'll have more time to hatch specific plans.<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
At the same time, I could also crank up the effectiveness of keys and bonuses overall, to make them a little more significant, but<L.31.1>
that's really a separate issue. So basically there are three suggestions, the second of which I don't think I like already!<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
1. Should the three key players and three bonus players apply for all games, but with sliding effectiveness?<L.31.1>
2. Should the bonus skills apply for all games?<L.31.1>
3. Should the overall effectiveness of key players and bonus players be cranked up?<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
Comments are welcome - I think no.1 will be more realistic, as well as giving you more decisions points to make (it'd also make it<L.31.1>
rather more viable to key opposition pitchers, because there's much less worry about keying a pitcher who then doesn't play<L.31.1>
because your opponent has juggled his rotation) and more control over what can happen in the playoffs.<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
<Z>What are Keys? <C> One of the things the comment so far has shown up is that not many people seem to understand what I intend<L.31.1>
keys to simulate. Some people think they're almost meaningless, some seem to think they're like a voodoo curse on a player, some<L.31.1>
think they're a "game thing". All, I believe, are wrong. What keys are meant to simulate is your preparation for facing a<L.31.1>
particular opposition player. In real-life, on TV, they often show that Bloggs is 4-21 lifetime against Smith, without explaining<L.31.1>
why. It isn't because Bloggs stays awake at night worrying about Smith, it's more likely because Smith throws a low cutter, or a<L.31.1>
curve he can't hit. Good teams will figure this out, and when Bloggs is in the box, their pitchers will throw a higher mix of what<L.31.1>
he can't hit - reducing his effectiveness. That comes from scouting. It's actually easier to watch on TV with starting pitchers -<L.1.1>
<P>
<L>
<L.1.1>
you can watch a David Wells game and he'll throw curve after curve at one hitter, then none at the next. Partly he's "mixing it<L.31.1>
up", but mostly it's because he knows how well various people handle his pitching. The closest you'll generally see it commented<L.31.1>
on on TV is when a hitter is described as a "low ball hitter" or a "high ball hitter". Or "not good inside".<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
Gameplan Baseball isn't about "pitch-by-pitch" play, but this sort of preparation is something I think is relevant, and something<L.31.1>
that happens in real-life, albeit not very commented upon. A team have scouts who follow the opponents and produce scouting<L.31.1>
reports on how to beat certain players, depending on what they spot. That, for me, is what keys (and bonuses) are meant to<L.31.1>
simulate - an adjustment of your team's strengths and weaknesses according to those of your opponent.<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
<Z>Scouting Levels? <C> One "solution" to the differing perceptions (and interests!) in keys could be to introduce a scouting<L.31.1>
level. Similar to trainers levels, this would determine how effective your Bonus and Keys would actually be from week to week.<L.31.1>
Those coaches who want to invest minimal effort (and resources) in advanced scouting (ie tuning into Baseball today) can do so,<L.31.1>
and whilst their keys and bonuses would be relatively weak, they have more LPs to spend on players. Alternatively, you can spend<L.31.1>
to strengthen up their effect, but obviously you're taking away resources from other elements of your club.<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
I could even bring this in in conjunction with Hitting and Pitching coaches, who would have a low level effect on the performance<L.31.1>
of the whole of your team, and give you more management decisions about where to allocate the balance of your resources. Thoughts?<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
<Z>Recruiting <C> In the past we've offered a couple of free credits if you introduce someone new to one of our games. I'm now<L.31.1>
going to increase this "bounty" to five credits. It's becoming harder and harder to persuade new people to play PBM games, so it<L.31.1>
makes to try and increase the reward to encourage you guys to try and find more people to play the games, providing us with<L.31.1>
customers and you with opponents! Please be clear that this bonus is for recruiting NEW players - persuading someone to leave one<L.31.1>
league to join another, or move to Raceplan from Gameplan doesn't count. If you're on a chat forum for fans of your sport, or a<L.31.1>
member of a fan club and so forth, then preach the gospel and if people mention you when they join, we'll add the credits.<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
<Z>Late Email Results <C> If you think results are late, please make sure you wait until the following morning before chasing up<L.31.1>
results. First step is to check out the Latest News at www.pbmsports.com - if I am running late I'll post a notice there.<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
<Z>PDF Reports <C> Emailed game reports are now available for all games here. You should find PDF reports rather easier to cope<L.31.1>
with - Adobe Reader is free to download (see www.pbmsports.com for a link) and you can open your reports with one click of the<L.31.1>
mouse (indeed, you don't need a printer, though most of you will then print from it) and you don't need to worry about dodgy email<L.31.1>
clients (Hotmail and AOL are particularly common culprits) messing up the formatting, or printer drivers. The text format for<L.31.1>
emailed reports is still available but I only expect people will want to do so if they use the text file for other purposes (such<L.31.1>
as exporting the listings into some software you've produced yourself).<L.31.1>
<L.12.1>
If you've not tried email reports before, or you've had problems, try out the PDF. It really is very straightforward.<L.31.1>
